Impossible Attributes of the Messengers
Definition of impossible attributes for messengers and proof from transmitted evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four attributes that are impossible for messengers and why the proof of their impossibility is based on transmitted evidence rather than rational evidence.

Core Idea
Messengers cannot have traits opposite to their essential virtues, proven by revelation.

In this passage, the author lists the attributes that are inconceivable for prophets and messengers. After establishing their obligatory traits, he now identifies their opposites—such as betrayal and lying—which must be impossible. He also clarifies that our knowledge of this impossibility comes from transmitted sources (Quran, Sunnah, consensus) rather than from reason alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text slowly, noting the list of impossible traits and the phrase 'as they narrated'.
Pay attention to the contrast between obligatory and impossible.
2
Identify the four impossible attributes
List the four groups: betrayal, lying, dullness/heedlessness/lack of intelligence, and concealing the message.
The third attribute is expressed with three words: al-balaha, al-ghafla, 'adam al-fitna.
3
Understand the basis of proof
Notice the author says the relied-upon evidence is al-dalil al-sam'i (transmitted). Ask yourself: why might someone think it's rational? What does transmitting entail?
This clarifies the methodology of kalam.
4
Connect to the lesson objective
Relate this to the broader understanding of prophethood in Islamic theology: these impossibilities protect the integrity of the message.
The messengers are safeguarded by divine revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحيل في حقهم ضدها يعني: الصفات الأربعة الواجبة التي فرغ منها، وهي: الخيانة، والكذب، والبلاهة والغفلة وعدم الفطنة، وكتمان شيء مما أمروا بتبليغه. وأشار بقوله: (كما رووا) إلى أن المعول عليه في دليل امتناع ما ذكر عليهم إنما هو الدليل السمعي لا العقلي، أي حكمنا باستحالة ما ذكر في حقهم حكماً مماثلاً لما رواه العلماء ونقلوه كتاباً وسنة وإجماعاً.
And it is impossible in their right their opposite, meaning: the four obligatory attributes that were completed, which are: betrayal, lying, dullness and heedlessness and lack of intelligence, and concealing something of what they were commanded to convey. And he indicated by his saying: 'as they narrated' that the relied-upon in the proof of the impossibility of what was mentioned upon them is only the transmitted evidence, not the rational evidence. Meaning, we judge the impossibility of what was mentioned in their right as a judgment similar to what the scholars narrated and transmitted from Book, Sunnah, and consensus.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage defines the attributes that are impossible for the messengers. It first lists them: the opposites of the four obligatory attributes (trustworthiness, truthfulness, intelligence, and conveying the message). Specifically: treason (al-khiyana), lying (al-kidhb), dullness/heedlessness/lack of intelligence (al-balaha, al-ghafla, 'adam al-fitna), and concealing any part of what they are commanded to convey (kitman). The passage then explains the basis for ruling these impossible: it is primarily transmitted evidence (al-dalil al-sam'i) rather than rational evidence, as the author indicates by the phrase 'as they narrated' (kama rawwaw). This means the judgment of impossibility is derived from what scholars have transmitted from the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.

Fainting, Madness, Blindness, and Forgetfulness in Prophets
Clarification of permissible and impermissible states for prophets regarding health and memory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which physical and mental states are permissible for prophets and which are impossible, based on the distinction between disease and deficiency.

Core Idea
Disease is permissible for prophets; deficiency is not.

The question of which human experiences can touch prophets is a delicate one. Scholars distinguish between temporary ailments that do not detract from their station and permanent deficiencies that contradict their perfection. This passage from al-Sanusi clarifies four key states: fainting, madness, blindness, and forgetfulness, showing how each is judged by whether it is a disease or a deficiency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Note the four states mentioned.
2
Identify the key distinction
The passage uses two criteria: disease (marad) and deficiency (naqs). Understand why fainting is classified as the former and madness as the latter.
3
Examine the special case of forgetfulness
Forgetfulness is said to be impossible only in 'communicative reports' (akhbar balaghiyya). Reflect on why that distinction matters for prophecy.
Forgetfulness in other matters may be possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا شك في جواز الإغماء عليهم؛ لأنه مرض، والمرض يجوز عليهم، بخلاف الجنون قليله وكثيره؛ لأنه نقص، ويلحق به العمى، ولم يعم نبي قط، ولم يثبت أن شعيباً كان ضريراً، ويعقوب إنما حصلت له غشاوة وزالت. وأما السهو فهو ممتنع عليهم في الأخبار البلاغية، وغيرها كالأقوال.
And there is no doubt in the permissibility of fainting upon them, because it is a disease, and disease is permissible upon them, unlike madness, its little and its much, because it is a deficiency. And blindness is attached to it, and no prophet ever became blind, and it has not been established that Shu'ayb was blind, and Jacob only had a covering over his eyes which then disappeared. And as for forgetfulness, it is impossible upon them in the communicative reports, and other things like statements.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage addresses various physical and mental states with respect to prophets. First, fainting (ighma') is permissible because it is a disease, and diseases are permissible for prophets. This is contrasted with madness (junun), whether minor or major, which is impossible because it is a deficiency (naqs). The passage then adds blindness (ama) to the category of what is impossible: no prophet ever became blind, and the claim about Shu'ayb being blind is not established; Jacob's condition was a temporary covering that later disappeared. Finally, forgetfulness (sahw) is discussed: it is impossible for prophets in matters of conveying revelation (al-akhbar al-balaghiyya), i.e., the reports they are commanded to deliver, but in other matters (like ordinary statements) it may be possible. The passage maintains precision in distinguishing between categories of imperfection.

الأخبار البلاغية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might assume that fainting and forgetfulness are similar to madness or are always impermissible.
Correction: Fainting is a disease and thus permissible; forgetfulness is only impossible in conveying revelation, not in all matters.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Fainting is permissible as a disease, while madness and blindness are impossible as deficiencies; forgetfulness is impossible only in conveying revelation.

Impossible Attributes of Prophets and Their Transmitted Proof
Al-Bajuri enumerates impossible prophetic attributes and their transmitted proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the attributes that are impossible for prophets, why their proof is transmitted rather than rational, and the specific rulings on fainting, madness, and blindness.

Core Idea
The impossibility of prophetic opposites is a revealed certainty, not a rational deduction.

Al-Bajuri continues his discussion of rational judgments concerning prophets by addressing the attributes that are impossible for them—the opposites of trustworthiness, truthfulness, intelligence, and conveyance. These include betrayal, lying, stupidity, and concealment. He emphasizes that the proof for their impossibility is not rational but transmitted through revelation, consensus, and prophetic tradition. He then clarifies exceptions: fainting is permissible as an illness, while madness and blindness are impossible due to their inherent deficiency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impossible attributes
Read the passage and list the four opposite attributes that are impossible for prophets: betrayal, lying, stupidity/heedlessness, and concealment of the message.
These are the opposites of the four obligatory attributes.
2
Understand the source of proof
Notice that Al-Bajuri explicitly says the proof is transmitted (سمعي) from Book, Sunnah, and consensus, not rational. Consider why this distinction is important.
This guards against over-reliance on mere reason.
3
Examine specific conditions
Identify the rulings on fainting, madness, and blindness. Fainting is permissible because it is an illness; madness is impossible because it is a deficiency; blindness is annexed to madness.
Historical examples of Jacob and Shu'ayb are given.
4
Reflect on the principle
Ask yourself why only transmitted evidence can prove these negatives, and how this preserves the prophetic station.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
م شرع في ثاني أقسام الحكم العقليّ المُتعلقة بالرُّسل عليهم السلام، فقال: (وَيَسْتَحِيلُ) في حَقِّهم (ضِدُّهَا) يعني: الصفات الأربعة الواجبة التي فرغ منها، وهي: الخيانة، والكذب، والبلاهة والغفلة وعدم الفطنة، وكتمان شيء مما أمروا بتبليغه، وأشار بقوله: (كَمَا رَوَوْا) إلى أنَّ المُعوّل عليه في دليل امتناع ما ذكر عليهم إن هو الدَّليلُ السَّمعي لا العقلي، أي حكمنا باستحالة ما ذُكر في حقهم حكماً مماثلاً لما رواه العلماء ونقلوه كتاباً وسُنَّة وإجماعاً. ولا شكّ في جواز الإغماء عليهم؛ لأنَّه مرض، والمرض يجوز عليهم، بخلاف الجنون قليله وكثيره؛ لأنَّه نقص، ويُلحق به العَمى، ولم يَعْمَ نبي قطُّ، ولم يثبت أنَّ شُعيباً كان ضريرا، ويعقوبُ إنَّما حصلت له غِشاوة وزالت.
He began the second section of rational judgments related to the prophets, peace be upon them, and said: 'And impossible for them is their opposite' meaning: the four obligatory attributes which he completed, namely: betrayal, lying, stupidity, heedlessness, lack of acumen, and concealing anything they were commanded to convey. And he indicated by his saying: 'as they narrated' that the relied-upon evidence for forbidding what was mentioned about them is only transmitted evidence, not rational evidence, meaning we rule the impossibility of what was mentioned regarding them as a ruling similar to what the scholars narrated and transmitted as Book, Sunnah, and consensus. And there is no doubt about the permissibility of fainting for them because it is an illness, and illness is permissible for them, unlike madness, whether little or much, because it is a deficiency, and blindness is annexed to it, and no prophet ever became blind, and it is not confirmed that Shu'ayb was blind, and Jacob only had a covering over his eyes which lifted.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage defines the attributes impossible for prophets. It begins by explaining that the poet's phrase 'their opposite' refers to the opposites of the four obligatory attributes: trustworthiness, truthfulness, intelligence, and conveyance. These opposites are specifically betrayal, lying, stupidity/heedlessness, and concealment of the message. The proof for their impossibility is not rational but transmitted (سمعي), relying on the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. The commentator then discusses fainting: it is permissible for prophets because it is an illness, which does not detract from their status. However, madness is impossible because it implies deficiency. Blindness is similarly impossible; no prophet was ever blind, though Jacob's temporary loss of sight is explained as a covering that lifted. The passage emphasizes that the evidence is primarily from revelation, not mere reason.

?
If the prophets are protected from lying and stupidity, their message is perfectly reliable. Have you been treating the Prophet's message (peace be upon him) as the absolute truth in your daily life, or do you pick and choose based on convenience? What is one command from the Sunnah that you have been neglecting, and will you obey it starting today?
?
The passage distinguishes between permissible illnesses like fainting and impossible defects like madness. How does this affect your view of the Prophet's humanity? Do you sometimes forget that he was a human being with normal human experiences, or do you fall into extremes of either exaggerating or diminishing his status? Reflect on how you can love him as both a human and a messenger.

Forgetfulness in Prophets: Statements vs Actions
Al-Bajuri classifies forgetfulness in prophets into impossible and permissible categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between forgetfulness in prophetic statements (impossible) and actions (permissible) and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from forgetfulness in conveying revelation but not in all actions.

Al-Bajuri addresses a nuanced aspect of prophetic infallibility: forgetfulness (sahw). While prophets are immune from error in delivering the divine message, they may experience forgetfulness in certain actions. This passage defines the boundaries clearly, distinguishing between statements and actions and providing the rationale.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two categories: what is impossible (ممتنع) and what is permissible (يجوز).
The passage is dense; take time to identify each term.
2
Identify the distinction
Pinpoint what is impossible: reports of delivery (الأخبار البلاغية) and religious constructive statements (الأقوال الدينية الإنشائية). What is permissible: actions of delivery (الأفعال البلاغية) and other actions.
The key is the difference between conveying information (statements) and demonstrating practice (actions).
3
Reflect on the wisdom
Consider why forgetfulness is permissible in actions but not in conveying the message. The commentary explains that it allows for teaching through demonstration, as occurred when the Prophet mistakenly gave salaam after two rak'ahs.
This shows that prophetic infallibility is purposeful, protecting revelation while allowing human experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكمُ السَّهو والنسيان من الأنبياء. وأمَّا السَّهو فهو ممتنع عليهم في الأخبار البلاغية، وغيرها كالأقوال الدينيَّة الإنشائيَّة، ويجوز في الأفعال البلاغيَّة وغيرها.
The ruling on forgetfulness (sahw) and forgetfulness (nisyan) from the prophets. As for sahw (forgetfulness/error), it is impossible for them in the reports of delivery (al-akhbar al-balaghah) and others like religious constructive statements (al-aqwal al-diniyyah al-insha'iyyah), and it is permissible in actions of delivery (al-af'al al-balaghah) and others.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage defines the ruling on forgetfulness (السَّهو) in prophets. It begins by stating that sahw is impossible (ممتنع) in matters related to delivering divine revelation (الأخبار البلاغية) — i.e., when a prophet is conveying a message from Allah about matters of belief or law. It is also impossible in other types of statements, specifically religious constructive utterances (الأقوال الدينية الإنشائية) such as commands and prohibitions. However, sahw is permissible (يجوز) in actions related to delivery (الأفعال البلاغية), meaning actions that demonstrate the practice of the religion, such as prayer — as occurred when the Prophet mistakenly gave salaam after two rak'ahs. It is also permissible in other actions not directly related to delivery. The distinction hinges on whether the error affects the correct transmission of the message: when error occurs in conveying information, it is impossible; when it occurs in practical demonstration, it is permissible due to the wisdom of teaching through stronger demonstration.

Key Terms
السهو
الأخبار البلاغية
الأقوال الدينية الإنشائية
الأفعال البلاغية
ممتنع
يجوز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think all forgetfulness is impossible for prophets.
Correction: The passage clarifies that sahw in actions (including actions of delivery) is permissible, while only sahw in statements directly conveying revelation or religious injunctions is impossible.

Checkpoint
In what type of prophetic action is forgetfulness (sahw) permissible according to this passage?
A) In delivering Quranic verses
B) In issuing religious rulings
C) In actions of delivery (such as prayer)
D) In conveying prophetic traditions

Key Takeaway
Prophets are infallible in conveying revelation but not in all actions; forgetfulness in practical demonstrations is permissible to facilitate teaching.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a mistake in your prayer or other act of worship, do you feel shame that prevents you from learning, or do you accept it as part of human nature and use it to improve? How does the Prophet's forgetfulness in prayer guide you to respond to your own slips?
?
If a teacher or leader you respect makes an honest mistake in teaching you about faith, do you lose trust in them completely? How does this lesson's distinction between errors in conveying the message and errors in practical demonstration shape your expectations?
?
Are there areas in your life where you demand perfection from yourself, only to be paralyzed by failure? How can the principle that even prophets are not expected to be perfect in all actions free you to strive without despair?

Forgetfulness in Prophets: The Three Rulings
Al-Bajuri distinguishes nisyan before and after the delivery of revelation and abrogated rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three distinct rulings on prophetic forgetfulness: before delivery, after delivery, and regarding abrogated rulings.

Core Idea
Prophetic forgetfulness is only impossible during active transmission of revelation.

This lesson explores a nuanced aspect of prophetic infallibility: the permissibility of forgetfulness in certain contexts. Al-Bajuri carefully distinguishes between the time before and after conveying revelation, and also addresses abrogated rulings. Understanding these distinctions is key to appreciating the scope of prophetic protection from error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the full English translation. Notice the key terms: النسيان, البلاغيات, قبل التبليغ, بعد التبليغ, المنسوخ.
The passage is short but packed with legal nuance.
2
Identify the three cases
The passage presents three distinct situations regarding forgetfulness. List each one and note whether it is impossible (ممتنع) or permissible (يجوز) and the condition (قبل/بعد التبليغ, مطلقا).
Use the guided breakdown below to see the structure.
3
Understand the rationale
Ask: Why is forgetfulness impossible before delivery but permissible after? What is the role of preservation? Why is abrogated matter always permissible to forget?
The commentary explains the reasoning behind each ruling.
4
Reflect on implications for prophetic infallibility
Consider how this teaching affects our understanding of 'isma (infallibility). Does it limit it? How does it reconcile with the need for reliable transmission?
This connects to broader doctrines of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا النسيان فهو ممتنع في البلاغيَّات قبل تبليغها قولية كانت أو فعليّة، وأمَّا بعد التبليغ فيجوز نسيانُ ما ذُكر عليهم، لحفظه بعد التبليغ، ووجوب ضبطه على المُبلّغ ليعمل به وليبلغه، ولا يمتنع عليهم نسيان المنسوخ مُطلقا، لا قبل التبليغ ولا بعده.
As for forgetfulness (nisyan), it is impossible in the matters of delivery (al-balaghiyat) before they are conveyed, whether they are verbal or actional. But after conveyance, it is permissible for them to forget what was mentioned to them, due to its preservation after conveyance, and the obligation of the one who conveys to retain it in order to act by it and convey it. And it is not impossible for them to forget the abrogated matter (al-mansukh) absolutely, neither before nor after conveyance.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage defines the ruling on forgetfulness (النسيان) in prophets. It classifies three situations: (1) Forgetfulness in matters of delivering revelation (البلاغيات) is impossible (ممتنع) before the act of conveying them, whether the delivery is verbal (e.g., a verse or ruling) or actional (e.g., demonstrating a prayer). This is because the prophet must perfectly recall the message to deliver it accurately. (2) After the message has been conveyed, forgetfulness is permissible (يجوز), because the message has already been preserved in the hearts and records of the community, and the prophet's personal recall is no longer necessary for its preservation. However, it remains obligatory for the messenger to recall it initially to act upon it and to convey it to others. (3) As for matters that are abrogated (المنسوخ), forgetfulness is never impossible, whether before or after their conveyance, because they are no longer operative. The passage carefully delineates the scope of prophetic infallibility regarding memory, showing that it is limited to the period of active transmission but not after.

Key Terms
النسيان
البلاغيات
قولية
فعلية
قبل التبليغ
بعد التبليغ
ضبط
المنسوخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that prophets are immune to forgetfulness in all circumstances.
Correction: The passage shows that forgetfulness after delivery is permissible, and for abrogated rulings it is always permissible.

Checkpoint
When is forgetfulness (nisyan) impossible for prophets?
A) After conveying the message
B) In abrogated rulings
C) Before conveying matters of delivery
D) In any action

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from forgetfulness only before delivering revelation; after delivery it is permissible, and abrogated rulings are always permissible to forget.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If prophets are allowed to forget after conveying the message, how much more should we, who are not infallible, be cautious about remembering and acting on what we have learned? What steps will you take this week to ensure you do not forget the essential truths you have received?
?
The passage shows that forgetfulness of abrogated rulings is permissible because they no longer apply. Are you still holding onto outdated understandings or practices that should have been left behind? What one thing do you need to 'forget' in order to follow Allah's guidance more faithfully?
?
The prophet had the responsibility to retain the message to act by it and convey it. Are you treating the knowledge you have as a sacred trust to be lived and shared, or as mere information? What would change if you saw every truth you know as something you are obligated to embody and pass on?

The Ruling on Forgetfulness and Oversight in Prophets (General Ruling)
Enumeration of rulings on forgetfulness and oversight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the categories of forgetfulness and oversight in prophets: which are permissible and which are impossible, and why.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from forgetfulness only in delivering revelation; after delivery, forgetfulness is permissible.

This lesson clarifies the theological ruling on forgetfulness and oversight among prophets. Contrary to a common assumption that prophets never forget anything, the text explains that forgetfulness is only impossible in matters directly related to the communication of revelation. In other contexts, it is permissible. Let us examine the precise boundaries drawn by the author.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author makes a key distinction between سهو and نسيان.
2
Identify the three key rulings
The passage presents the permissibility of سهو, the impossibility of نسيان before delivery, and its permissibility after delivery. Also note the ruling on the abrogated.
Forgetfulness of the abrogated is permissible both before and after delivery.
3
Reflect on the wisdom behind the ruling
Ask yourself why forgetfulness after delivery is allowed. The text says it is for preservation and to show that the prophet's perfection is from Allah, not intrinsic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكمُ السَّهو والنسيان من الأنبياء الدينيَّة الإنشائيَّة، ويجوز في الأفعال البلاغيَّة وغيرها. وأمَّا النسيان فهو ممتنع في البلاغيَّات قبل تبليغها قولية كانت أو فعليّة، وأمَّا بعد التبليغ فيجوز نسيانُ ما ذُكر عليهم، لحفظه بعد التبليغ، ووجوب ضبطه على المُبلّغ ليعمل به وليبلغه، ولا يمتنع عليهم نسيان المنسوخ مُطلقا، لا قبل التبليغ ولا بعده. بمعنى أنه يستحيل عليهم أن يسهوا بحيث يخبروا بخلاف الواقع، كأن يقول: الجنة تفنى. فإن قلت: قد ورد أنه له مرَّ على جماعة يؤبرون النخل وقال لهم: «لو تركتموها لصلحت» فتركوها فشاصت وخرجت التمر رديئة؛ فالجواب: أن هذا ليس من باب الإخبار، بل هو من قبيل الإنشاء، أي: كان في رجائي ذلك، والإنشاء لا يتعلق به تصديق ولا تكذيب، وعدم وقوع الشيء المرتجى لا يُعد نقصا. وأما نسيان الشيطان فمستحيل عليهم؛ إذ ليس للشيطان عليهم سبيل. قال تعالى: سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنسَى إِلَّا مَا شَاءَ الله [الأعلى ٧].
The ruling on oversight and forgetfulness from the prophets concerning religious enactments, and it is permissible in communicative actions and others. As for forgetfulness, it is impossible in the communicative matters before their delivery, whether verbal or actual. As for after delivery, it is permissible for them to forget what was mentioned to them, for its preservation after delivery, and the obligation of mastering it for the one who delivers so that he may act by it and deliver it. And forgetfulness of the abrogated is not impossible for them absolutely, neither before delivery nor after. That is, it is impossible for them to be forgetful to the extent that they inform contrary to reality, such as saying: Paradise will perish. If you say: It has been reported that he passed by a group pollinating date palms and said to them: 'If you leave them, they will be fine,' so they left them and they became spoiled and produced bad dates. The answer: This is not from the category of informing, but rather from the category of construction, i.e., it was in my hope and expectation. Construction does not involve verification or falsification, and the non-occurrence of the hoped thing is not considered a deficiency. And forgetfulness by Satan is impossible for them, for Satan has no way over them. He said: 'We will make you recite, so you shall not forget, except what Allah wills' [al-A'la 87:7].
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings on oversight (سهو) and forgetfulness (نسيان) among prophets. It begins by stating that oversight in religiously enacted actions is permissible, and also in communicative actions. Forgetfulness is then divided into two categories: before and after delivering the message. Before delivery, forgetfulness in matters that constitute the message (both verbal and actual) is impossible, because the prophet must reliably convey the revelation. After delivery, forgetfulness of what was mentioned is permissible, as a means of preserving it and demonstrating that the prophet's perfection is not intrinsic but from Allah. The passage also addresses an objection regarding an incident where the Prophet (peace be upon him) advised leaving date palms alone and the result was bad fruit. The answer clarifies that this was not an informative statement but an expression of opinion or hope, which is not subject to truth or falsehood, and thus not a defect. Finally, it states that Satan cannot cause prophets to forget, citing the Quranic verse that the Prophet only forgets what Allah wills.

Key Terms
سهو
نسيان
تبليغ
منسوخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets cannot forget anything at all.
Correction: The text teaches that forgetfulness is only impossible in delivering revelation; after delivery, it is permissible.

Checkpoint
In which scenario is forgetfulness absolutely impossible for a prophet?
A) After delivering the message
B) Before delivering any message that constitutes part of revelation
C) In matters of abrogated rulings
D) In any context

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from forgetfulness only in the actual delivery of revelation; after that, forgetfulness is permissible and even serves divine wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that prophets were allowed to forget after delivering the message. Have you ever heard a truth about Allah but then let it slip from your mind, treating it as if it were optional? What is one specific teaching from the Quran or Sunnah that you have forgotten to apply, and what will you do today to reclaim it?
?
The passage says prophets can forget abrogated rulings. This shows that their perfection lies in delivering the message, not in perfect memory. Are you more focused on memorising facts about religion or on truly living the message that has been delivered? Which area of your obedience have you been careless about, thinking that hearing it once is enough?
?
If prophets could forget after delivering, how much more careful must you be to preserve what you have learned? What is one action you will take this week to ensure that a critical lesson from this module does not become forgotten in your daily life?

The Objection of the Date Palm and Satanic Forgetfulness
Objection and answer regarding a prophetic statement about date palms and the impossibility of satanic forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between informative and injunctive statements in the context of prophetic forgetfulness, and why Satan cannot cause prophets to forget.

Core Idea
A prophet's opinion-based statement is not a defect, and Satan has no power to make a prophet forget.

The second part of the passage addresses a potential objection: a report that the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave advice about date palms that turned out to be inaccurate. The author explains that this was not an informative statement but an expression of hope or opinion. The lesson also concludes that Satan cannot influence prophets in matters of forgetfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Carefully read the objection about the date palms and the author's response. Pay attention to the distinction made.
The distinction is between إخبار (informing) and إنشاء (construction/opinion).
2
Understand the key distinction
Note that إنشاء does not involve truth or falsehood. The non-occurrence of the hoped thing is not a deficiency.
This protects the prophet from being accused of error.
3
Reflect on satanic forgetfulness
Read the final part about Satan and the verse. Understand that Satan cannot cause prophets to forget.
The verse proves that forgetfulness only occurs by Allah's will.

Defining Permissible (جائز) Actions for Prophets
Definition of the permissible (جائز) category for prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational category of 'permissible' (جائز) as it applies to prophets, including its definition and its dual permissibility by reason and law.

Core Idea
Permissible actions for prophets are those that reason neither requires nor prohibits.

Before we examine specific examples, we must establish what it means for an action to be 'permissible' for a prophet. This lesson introduces the core definition of the third rational judgment—the permissible (جائز)—as applied to prophets. The passage below, from the section on prophethood, defines this category and sets the stage for the examples that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to get the author's full meaning.
Pay attention to the structure: first the definition, then the ruling.
2
Identify the definition of جائز
The passage defines جائز as 'that which is not rationally necessary nor rationally negated' for prophets. Note the two key conditions: neither wajib nor mustahil.
3
Understand the dual permission
The passage says permissible actions are 'rationally and legally' (عقلاً وشرعاً) allowed. Consider why both aspects are mentioned.
This shows that kalam considers both reason and revelation.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: Why is it important to establish a third category of permissible actions before giving examples? How does this prevent extremes in understanding prophethood?
This guards against both over-restriction and over-permissiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم النبوات ما يجوز عقلاً في حق الرُّسُل الكرام. وَجَائِزٌ فِي حَقِّهِمْ كَالأَكْلِ وَكَالجِماعِ لِلنِّسا في الحِل. وهو: ما لم يجب عند العقل ثبوته لهم ولا نفيه عنهم، بل يصح عنده وجوده لهم وعدمه؛ فيجوز عقلا وشرعاً في حَقِّهِمْ أي: الرُّسل عليهم الصَّلاة والسَّلام أجمعين خُصوصاً سيدهم الأعظم كَالأَكْلِ والشُّرب الحلال، والنَّوم مِن كُلِّ عَرَضٍ بَشري ليس مُحرَّمًا مكروها، ولا مُباحًا مُزْريًا، ولا مُؤْمِنًا، ولا ممَّا تَعافُهُ الأَنْفُسُ، ولا ممَّا يؤدّي إلى النفرة، سواء كان من توابع الصّحة ولا يُستغنى عنه عادةً كما مثل به، أو يُستغنى عنه كالجِمَاعِ لِلنِّسَا بناءً على أنَّه مِن باب التّفكه، أو بحبس النَّفس عنه بناءً على أنَّه مِن باب القُوت؛ فيجوز عليهم وطء النِّساء بالملك مُطلقا مسلماتٍ أو كتابيَّات لا كمجوسيَّات وبالنكاح ما عدا الكتابية والمجوسية، وما عدا الأمة ولو مسلمةٌ؛ لأنَّها إِنَّما تُنكِحُ لخوف العَنَتِ أو عدم الطَّوّل، والثَّاني منتف بالبديهة، والأوَّل كذلك للعصمة.
Section on prophecies: What is rationally permissible concerning the noble messengers. And permissible in their right is like eating and like sexual intercourse with women in that which is lawful. And it is that which is not rationally necessary for them nor rationally negated from them, rather their existence or absence is rationally valid; thus it is permissible rationally and legally concerning them—i.e., the messengers, peace be upon them all, especially their greatest master—like lawful eating and drinking, sleep, from every human accident that is not forbidden, disliked, nor an abominable permissible, nor harmful, nor from that which souls abhor, nor from that which leads to aversion. Whether it is from the accompaniments of health and not customarily dispensable, as he gave an example, or it is dispensable like sexual intercourse with women, on the basis that it is from the category of enjoyment, or by self-restraint (holding back) on the basis that it is from the category of sustenance. So sexual intercourse with women by ownership is absolutely permissible for them, whether Muslim women or women of the book, but not Magians, and by marriage except the woman of the book and the Magian, and except the slave woman even if she is Muslim, because she is married only for fear of hardship or lack of financial ability; the second is obvious, and the first likewise due to infallibility (عصمة).
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of rational judgment concerning prophets: the permissible (جائز). It states that permissible actions are those which reason does not deem necessary for them nor impossible, but rather their occurrence or non-occurrence is equally valid. Such actions are permissible both rationally and legally. The author then lists examples: lawful eating, drinking, sleeping, and every human attribute that is not forbidden, disliked, abominable, harmful, repugnant, or leading to aversion. These can be either indispensable (like eating) or dispensable (like sexual intercourse). For sexual relations, prophets may have intercourse with women they own, regardless of religion except Magians, and by marriage with free Muslim women, but not with women of the book or slave women. The reason given is that marriage to a slave woman is only permitted for fear of hardship (العنت) or lack of financial means (عدم الطول), both of which are impossible for prophets due to their infallibility and divine provision.

Key Terms
جائز
حكم عقلي
وجوب
استحالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prophets cannot engage in any human activities like eating or marriage.
Correction: This passage shows that such actions are permissible (جائز) both rationally and legally, as long as they do not contradict their infallibility or dignity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best defines a جائز action for prophets?
A) An action that is obligatory for them
B) An action that is impossible for them
C) An action that reason neither requires nor negates
D) An action that is only legally permissible but not rational

Key Takeaway
The permissible (جائز) category allows prophets to perform ordinary human acts that reason does not require or prohibit, so long as they are lawful and dignified.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the Prophet's ordinary human acts (eating, marriage), does it bring him closer to you or create a sense of distance? What does your reaction reveal about your own struggle to follow his example in mundane matters?
?
If you truly believed that the Prophet's permissible actions were intentionally preserved as guidance, how would you change your approach to your own daily lawful activities—from eating to sleeping? What is one small change you can commit to this week?
?
The passage shows that reason and revelation agree on the permissibility of certain prophetic acts. In what area of your life do you feel a tension between reason and revelation? What would it take for you to seek that harmony rather than avoid it?

Examples and Conditions of Permissible Actions for Prophets
Enumeration of examples and conditions for permissible actions of prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the key examples of permissible actions for prophets (eating, drinking, sleep) and understand the conditions that make an action permissible rather than degrading.

Core Idea
Permissible actions are those that are not forbidden, disliked, abominable, harmful, repugnant, or causing aversion.

Having defined the permissible category, the author now gives concrete examples. This lesson explores the specific actions that are permissible for prophets—like lawful eating and sleeping—and the detailed conditions that ensure these actions do not compromise their dignity or prophetic status. The passage also distinguishes between indispensable and dispensable actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of examples
Read the Arabic passage and identify the actions mentioned: eating, drinking, sleep, and every human attribute. Note the qualifying conditions.
The list is not exhaustive but illustrative.
2
Understand the negative conditions
The passage lists what permissible actions must not be: haram, makruh, mubah muzri, mu'min (harmful), repugnant to souls, or leading to aversion. Understand each term briefly.
'Mubah muzri' means a permissible act that is degrading. 'Mu'min' likely means harmful (based on context).
3
Distinguish indispensable vs. dispensable
The passage divides permissible actions into two types: those that are accompaniments of health and not customarily dispensable (like eating), and those that are dispensable (like sexual intercourse). Note the rationale given for each.
This classification helps understand why some actions are more essential than others.

Detailed Rulings on Marriage and Sexual Relations for Prophets
Detailed rulings on permissible sexual relations for prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific rules regarding prophets' sexual relations, especially the permissibility of intercourse with slave women, and the limitations on marriage with women of the book and slave women.

Core Idea
Prophets may have sexual relations with lawful women they own, but marriage to slave women is prohibited due to their infallibility.

The previous lesson mentioned sexual intercourse as a permissible but dispensable action. Now the author provides detailed juridical rulings on prophets' sexual relations, specifying what forms of union are allowed and which are not. This passage clarifies the intersection of prophetic dignity, legal categories of marriage and ownership, and the principle of infallibility (عصمة).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on rulings
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the distinction between 'intercourse by ownership' (وطء بالملك) and 'intercourse by marriage' (وطء بالنكاح).
These are two different legal bases for sexual relations.
2
Understand the exceptions
Identify which women are excluded: for marriage, women of the book and slave women even if Muslim. For ownership, only Magians are excluded. Ask why.
The reasons relate to the conditions for marrying a slave woman (fear of hardship, lack of means) which do not apply to prophets.
3
Connect to infallibility (عصمة)
The passage ends by stating that the conditions for marrying a slave woman are absent 'due to infallibility' (للعصمة). Consider how prophets' lack of material need and moral purity justify these restrictions.

The Permissible (Ja'iz) for Prophets: Definition and Examples
Explanation of permissible acts for prophets with examples and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what constitutes a permissible (ja'iz) act for prophets, including its definition, examples, and the conditions that safeguard their prophetic dignity.

Core Idea
Prophets are fully human outwardly but divinely protected inwardly; their permissible actions reflect this balance.

This lesson examines the third rational judgment concerning prophets: the permissible (ja'iz). Drawing from classical Ash'ari theology, we explore what acts are allowed for prophets, why they are permitted, and how their outward humanity coexists with their inward protection from sin. The passage defines ja'iz, lists examples like eating and sleeping, and outlines specific restrictions, especially regarding sexual relations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without heavy analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author's own structure guide your understanding.
Notice the technical terms like 'ja'iz' and 'rusul'.
2
Identify the definition of ja'iz
Find the definition: 'that which reason does not necessitate affirming for them nor negating from them.' Understand that both existence and non-existence are rationally possible for prophets.
3
Examine the examples and restrictions
List the examples given: eating lawful food, drinking, sleeping, and sexual intercourse. Note the conditions for sexual intercourse: only in a state of permissibility, not during fasting, menstruation, etc.
The passage details six prohibited states for intercourse.
4
Understand the outward/inward distinction
The passage concludes by separating outward (zawahir) human experiences from inward (bawatin) purity. Prophets are human in outward matters like health changes, but inwardly protected (ma'sum) from sin and connected to angels.
This distinction resolves potential confusion about prophetic humanity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار إلى ثالث أقسام الحكم العقليّ المُتعلقة بالأنبياء والرسل عليهم الصَّلاة والسَّلام بقوله : (وَجَائِزُ) وهو : ما لم يجب عند العقل ثبوته لهم ولا نفيه عنهم، بل يصح عنده وجوده لهم وعدمه ؛ فيجوز عقلا وشرعاً (في حَقِّهِمْ) أي: الرُّسل عليهم الصَّلاة والسَّلام أجمعين خُصوصاً سيدهم الأعظم ( كَالأَكْلِ والشُّرب الحلال ، والنَّوم .. مِن كُلِّ عَرَضٍ بَشري ليس مُحرَّمًا مكروها ، ولا مُباحًا مُزْريًا ، ولا مُؤْمِنًا ، ولا ممَّا تَعافُهُ الأَنْفُسُ ، ولا ممَّا يؤدّي إلى النفرة، سواء كان من توابع الصّحة ولا يُستغنى عنه عادةً كما مثل به ، أو يُستغنى عنه كالجِمَاعِ لِلنِّسَا بناءً على أنَّه مِن باب التّفكه ، أو بحبس النَّفس عنه بناءً على أنَّه مِن باب القُوت ؛ فيجوز عليهم وطء النِّساء بالملك مُطلقا مسلماتٍ أو كتابيَّات لا كمجوسيَّات وبالنكاح ما عدا الكتابية والمجوسية، وما عدا الأمة ولو مسلمةٌ ؛ لأنَّها إِنَّما تُنكِحُ لخوف العَنَتِ أو عدم الطَّوّل ، والثَّاني منتف بالبديهة ، والأوَّل كذلك للعصمة ، كما أشار إليه بقوله (في) حال (الح) أي: الجواز ، لا في حال حُرمة ولا كراهة، ويَتبَعهُ أَنَّهم لا يَطؤُوهنَّ صائمات صوما مشروعا ، ولا معتكفاتٍ كذلك، ولا حائضات ، ولا في حَالِ نِفَاسٍ ولا إحرام، ولا في حال رؤيا واحتلام، ولمَّا كانوا من البشر وأرسلوا إلى البشر كانت ظواهرهم خالصة للبشرية، يجوز عليها من الآفات والتغيرات ما يجوز على البشر، وهذا لا نقيصة فيه، وأمَّا بواطنهم فمُنزَّهة غالبا عن ذلك معصومةٌ منه ، متعلقة بالملأ الأعلى والملائكة ؛ لأخذها عنهم وتلقيها الوحي منهم.
And he pointed to the third division of rational judgment related to the prophets and messengers, peace be upon them, with his statement: '(And permissible [ja'iz])' — that is: that which reason does not necessitate affirming for them nor negating from them, but rather its existence for them and its non-existence are both valid in reason; thus it is permissible rationally and legally in their right, i.e., the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them all, especially their greatest master, like eating and lawful drinking, and sleep, from every human accident that is not forbidden, disliked, nor permissible but degrading, nor harmful, nor from what souls abhor, nor from what leads to aversion, whether it is from the accompaniments of health and is not ordinarily dispensed with, as he exemplified, or is dispensed with like sexual intercourse with women, based on it being for pleasure, or by restraining the self from it based on it being for sustenance; so it is permissible for them to have intercourse with women by ownership absolutely, Muslims or Scriptural women, not Magians, and by marriage except the Scriptural and Magian, and except the slave woman even if Muslim; for she is only married for fear of hardship or lack of means; the second is obviously negated, and the first likewise because of protection (['isma] — عصمة), as he indicated by his statement 'in [the state of] permissibility', not in a state of prohibition or dislike; and it follows that they do not have intercourse with them while they are fasting a legitimate fast, nor while they are in i'tikaf likewise, nor while menstruating, nor in a state of postpartum bleeding nor ihram, nor in a state of dream or wet dream. And since they are human and were sent to humans, their outward aspects were purely human; what is permissible of afflictions and changes that befall humans is permissible upon them, and this is no deficiency. As for their inward aspects, they are generally purified of that, protected from it, connected to the highest assembly and the angels, because they receive revelation from them and take it from them.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage explains the category of 'ja'iz' (permissible) in rational judgment concerning prophets. It begins by recalling that rational judgments are of three types: wajib (necessary), ja'iz (permissible), and mustahil (impossible). The ja'iz is defined as that which reason does not necessitate as either existent or non-existent for the prophets; both possibilities are rationally valid. The commentator then clarifies that the term 'in their right' refers specifically to the messengers, with special mention of the Prophet Muhammad. The examples given are eating, lawful drinking, and sleep — every human incidental (arad) that is not forbidden (haram), disliked (makruh), permissible but degrading (mubah muzri), harmful (mu'dhi), or repulsive. The examples include both indispensable acts (like eating) and dispensable ones (like sexual intercourse), the latter being justified either as pleasure or as sustenance. The passage then discusses restrictions: prophets may not engage in intercourse during fasting, i'tikaf, menstruation, postpartum bleeding, ihram, or during dreams/wet dreams. Finally, the passage distinguishes between outward and inward states: outwardly, prophets are fully human and subject to permissible human experiences; inwardly, they are protected (ma'sum) from deficiencies and connected to the angelic realm for receiving revelation.

Key Terms
جائز (ja'iz)
رسل (rusul)
ظواهر (zawahir)
بواطن (bawatin)
عصمة ('isma)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are not truly human because they are sinless.
Correction: Prophets are fully human and experience permissible human needs like eating and sleeping; their sinlessness (isma) pertains to inward purity, not denial of human nature.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT permissible for prophets?
A) Eating lawful food
B) Sleeping
C) Engaging in sexual intercourse during menstruation
D) Drinking lawful drink

Key Takeaway
The permissible (ja'iz) for prophets includes all acts that reason allows and that do not contradict their prophetic dignity, exemplified by eating, sleeping, and lawful sexual relations under specific conditions, while their inward state remains divinely protected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that even the prophets' permissible actions—like eating and sleeping—were intentional and dignified. Consider your own daily habits: are you mindful of Allah's permission and boundaries in your routine? What one small permissible act will you consciously transform into an act of worship starting today?
?
The lesson teaches that prophets avoided even permissible acts in states that would compromise their spiritual state. Reflect: Is there a permissible activity in your life that you engage in while your heart is spiritually distracted or while neglecting a duty? How will you realign that action to be more like the prophetic example?
?
Prophets were protected from degrading acts even among halal options. Think about your own choices: do you ever settle for a permissible option that still feels lowly or unworthy of your spiritual status as a believer? What will you do to elevate your standards in one area this week?

Prophets: Human Outwardly, Pure Inwardly
The author explains the permissible human states of prophets and affirms their inner purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets experienced permissible human states while their inner selves were protected from sin and connected to the divine realm.

Core Idea
Prophets were fully human outwardly but flawlessly pure inwardly.

This lesson explores a key aspect of prophetic attributes: their complete humanity in outward, permissible matters, and their elevated inner purity. We will see how the author distinguishes between what is permissible (and therefore not a defect) and what is prohibited. The passage also clarifies that prophets' inward selves are protected and linked to the highest realm.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of permissibility
Notice that the discussion begins by clarifying that the permissibility regarding marital relations applies only in permissible cases, not prohibited or disliked situations.
This sets the legal framework for what follows.
2
Note the list of prohibited times
Identify the specific times when marital relations are not allowed: during a valid fast, i'tikaf, menstruation, postnatal bleeding, ihram, and during a dream or nocturnal emission.
These are six distinct prohibitions.
3
Observe the defense of prophetic humanity
The author asserts that prophets' outward aspects are purely human, so permissible human ailments and changes are not defects. This counters a potential misunderstanding that any human state would be beneath them.
The key point: such states are only problematic if prohibited, not inherently.
4
Grasp the outward-inward distinction
The passage contrasts the outward (purely human) with the inward (purified, protected, connected to angels). This shows the unique status of prophets: fully human in body, but spiritually elevated.
The inward purity is due to their reception of revelation from angels.

Commentary
This passage is a statement about the human states of prophets, particularly regarding permissibility of marital relations. It begins by explaining that the permissibility (jawaz) applies only in permissible cases, not in prohibited or disliked situations. It then lists specific prohibited times: during a valid fast, i'tikaf, menstruation, postnatal bleeding, ihram, and during a dream or nocturnal emission. The passage then defends that prophets are human: their outward appearances are purely human, so permissible human ailments and changes are not defects. However, their inward aspects (souls) are usually purified and protected from such base attributes, being connected to the highest realm and angels, as they receive revelation.

The Second Testimony Encompasses the Three Rational Judgments
Al-Sharnubi shows how the second shahada encompasses the three rational judgments regarding the prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second testimony (Muhammadun Rasul Allah) contains the three rational judgments (wajib, mustahil, jaiz) regarding the prophets.

Core Idea
The second shahada implies the three rational judgments about all prophets.

Al-Sharnubi explains that the declaration of Muhammad's prophethood is not isolated; it necessarily entails affirming everything he brought, including belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day. Moreover, it establishes the three rational judgments about the prophets themselves: their truthfulness is obligatory, lying is impossible, and human characteristics that do not detract from their status are possible. This passage thus shows the second testimony as a comprehensive foundation for prophetic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's flow.
Notice the compact style: the passage moves from general belief to specific judgments.
2
Identify the three rational judgments
Find the three categories: wujub al-sidq (obligation of truthfulness), istihalah al-khiyana wa al-kidhb (impossibility of betrayal and lying), and jawaz al-a'rad al-bashariyya (possibility of human accidents).
These correspond to wajib, mustahil, and jaiz.
3
Understand the entailment from the second testimony
Reflect on why affirming Muhammad's messengership requires believing in all previous prophets and their attributes. The passage argues that accepting his message means accepting everything he conveyed.
4
Connect to the broader framework
Realize that these three judgments are not arbitrary but are derived directly from the shahada itself, making it a concise foundation for prophetic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤخذ مِن الجملة الثَّانية : وجوب الإيمان بسائر الأنبياء والرسل والملائكة والكتب السَّماويّة واليوم الآخر وما فيه ؛ إذ التصريح برسالته يستلزم تصديقه في كلّ ما جاء به، ومن جملته ما ذُكر ، ويُعلم منه أيضا: وجوب صدقهم، واستحالة الخيانة والكذب عليهم، وجواز جميع الأعراض البشرية التي لا تُنقِصُ مراتبهم عليهم الصَّلاة والسلام، وهذه جملة أقسام الحكم العقلي المُتعلّقة بالرُّسل عليهم الصَّلاة والسَّلام ؛ ولهذا المعنى جعلهما الشارع
And from the second sentence is taken: the obligation of belief in all the prophets, messengers, angels, heavenly books, the Last Day, and what is in it; since the explicit mention of his messengership necessitates affirming him in everything he brought, and among that is what was mentioned. And from it is also known: the obligation of their truthfulness, the impossibility of betrayal and lying upon them, and the possibility of all human accidents that do not decrease their ranks, peace be upon them. And these are the divisions of rational judgment related to the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. And for this meaning the Legislator made them...
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage explains how the second testimony (Muhammadun Rasul Allah) contains the three rational judgments regarding the prophets. It states that from this testimony we derive the obligation (wujub) of believing in all prophets, messengers, angels, scriptures, the Last Day, and everything in it. This is because affirming Muhammad's messengership necessitates affirming whatever he brought, which includes these beliefs. Further, we derive the obligation of the prophets' truthfulness (wujub al-sidq), the impossibility of betrayal and lying (istihalah al-khiyana wa al-kidhb), and the possibility (jawaz) of all human accidents (a'rad bashariyya) that do not diminish their rank. The author then summarizes: these are the divisions of rational judgment (wajib, mustahil, jaiz) related to the messengers. The final sentence indicates that for this meaning the Lawgiver made the two testimonies (as the foundation of faith).

النبوة
الرسل
صدق النبي
استحالة الخيانة والكذب
جواز الأعراض البشرية
أقسام الحكم العقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The second testimony only affirms Muhammad's prophethood without entailing belief in all previous prophets and their attributes.
Correction: The passage shows that affirming Muhammad's messengership necessitates affirming everything he brought, including belief in all prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day, and also establishes the three rational judgments about prophets.

Checkpoint

A) Only the obligation of believing in Muhammad.
B) The obligation of believing in all prophets and angels and books and the Last Day.
C) The impossibility of miracles for prophets.
D) The possibility of lying for prophets.

Key Takeaway
The second testimony (Muhammadun Rasul Allah) is a comprehensive principle that entails belief in all prophetic teachings and establishes the three rational judgments about prophets: wajib (truthfulness), mustahil (infallibility from lying and betrayal), and jaiz (human characteristics that do not detract from their rank).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Prophethood: A Divine Gift, Not an Acquisition
The author defines prophethood and refutes its acquirability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the true definition of prophethood as a divine gift, why it cannot be acquired, and the key conditions that distinguish it from messengership.

Core Idea
Prophethood is pure divine favor, not a product of human effort or spiritual exercises.

This lesson tackles a fundamental creedal point: prophethood is not earned. The text begins by refuting philosophers who claimed it could be acquired through seclusion and worship. It then provides the precise legal definition of a prophet, outlining the qualifications and the relationship between prophethood and messengership. Understanding this distinction is crucial for a sound Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening refutation
Start by reading the verse line that declares prophethood is not acquired, even by the highest spiritual ascension. Notice the strong negation: 'lam takun nubuwwun muktasabah.'
This sets the tone against the philosophers.
2
Understand the philosophers' claim
The text explains that the philosophers allowed acquisition of prophethood through three practices: seclusion, worship, and consuming lawful food. Identify these three elements.
The refutation is the author's response.
3
Learn the definition of prophethood
Move to the definition: nubuwwa is Allah's inspiration to a rational, free, male human regarding a legislative obligatory ruling. Note each condition: rational, free, male, human.
This definition excludes women, slaves, and the insane.
4
Examine the optional conditions
The passage lists several 'whether or not' qualifications: whether he is commanded to convey, has a book, a new law, or abrogation. This shows prophethood is broader than messengership.
Messengership has the additional condition of being commanded to convey.
5
Review the comparison with risala
The final sentence says messengership is the same except for the requirement of conveyance. Reflect on how this clarifies the relationship between prophet (nabi) and messenger (rasul).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[تعريفُ النُّبوة، وبيان أنَّ النُّبوَّة محضُ تَفضُّلٍ مِن الله ] وَلَمْ تَكُنْ نُبُوَّةٌ مُكْتَسَبَهُ وَلَوْ رَقَى فِي الخَيرِ أَعْلَى عَقَبَهْ ولمَّا جوَّزَ الفلاسفةُ اكتساب النُّبوَّة بملازمة الخلوة والعبادة وتناول الحلال ، أشار إلى الرَّدِّ عليهم بقوله : (وَ) مذهب أهل الحق أَنَّه لَمْ تَكُنْ وهي ، نُبوَّة) شرعاً: إيحاء الله تعالى لإنسان عاقل حُرِّ ذَكرٍ، بحكم شرعي تكليفي، سواءٌ أمره بتبليغه أم لا ، كان معه كتاب أم لا ، كان له شرع مجدد أم لا ، كان له نسخ لشرع من قبله أو بعضه أم لا ، وكذا الرسالة إلا في اشتراط
[Definition of prophethood, and explanation that prophethood is pure favor from Allah] And prophethood was not acquired, even if one ascends in goodness to the highest peak. And when the philosophers allowed the acquisition of prophethood by adhering to seclusion, worship, and consuming lawful things, he pointed to the refutation of them by his saying: (And) the doctrine of the people of truth is that it is not, and it is, prophethood) legally: the inspiration of Allah the Exalted to a rational, free, male human being, with a legislative obligatory ruling, whether He commands him to convey it or not, whether he has a book or not, whether he has a new law or not, whether he has abrogation of a previous law or part of it or not. And likewise messengership except in requiring.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage defines prophethood (nubuwwa) and refutes the philosophers who claimed it could be acquired through effort. The author first cites the verse (from the poem) that 'prophethood was not acquired, even if one ascends to the highest peak in goodness.' Then he explains the context: the philosophers permitted acquiring prophethood by persistent seclusion, worship, and consuming lawful food. The poet refutes them by stating the doctrine of Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth) as follows: Prophethood legally (shar'an) is Allah's inspiration (ilha') to a rational, free, male human being, concerning a legislative obligatory ruling, whether or not he is commanded to convey it. The definition excludes women, slaves, and the insane. It also allows for variation: the prophet may or may not have a book, a new law, or abrogation of previous laws. The same definition applies to messengership (risala), except for the condition of conveyance (probably that a messenger is commanded to convey).

Key Terms
النبوة
الفلاسفة
الإيحاء
الحكم الشرعي التكليفي
الرسالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophethood can be earned by spiritual exercises.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that prophethood is purely a divine favor and cannot be acquired through seclusion, worship, or any human effort.

Checkpoint
According to the definition given, prophethood is characterized as:
A) Acquirable through worship and seclusion
B) Inspiration of Allah to a rational, free, male human
C) Only for those with a new law
D) Always requiring conveyance of the message

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is a divine gift defined as Allah's inspiration to a rational, free, male human with a legislative ruling, and it cannot be acquired through effort.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform acts of worship, do you ever feel that you are 'earning' Allah's favor? How does this lesson's claim that prophethood cannot be acquired challenge that mindset, and what does it mean for your reliance on deeds versus His mercy?
?
If prophethood is pure divine favor, what are the implications for your own spiritual efforts? Are you trusting in your own progress to get closer to Allah, or are you humbly relying on His choice?
?
This lesson refutes the idea that anyone can become a prophet through asceticism. In what ways might you subconsciously think you can 'climb' to Allah through your own piety? How can you today actively reject that prideful thought and instead thank Him for His unearned gifts?

Prophethood: A Divine Gift, Not Acquired
Sanusi defines prophethood and refutes the philosophical claim that it is acquired.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of prophethood in Islamic theology and why it is a pure divine gift, not something humans can acquire through effort.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a pure favor from Allah, not a prize for effort.

This lesson establishes the core Islamic belief that prophethood is a divine gift bestowed solely by Allah's will. The passage defines prophethood precisely and then refutes the philosophical claim that humans can acquire it through spiritual practices. Understanding this distinction is foundational to Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the author's argument emerge naturally.
Notice the two poetic verses that frame the discussion.
2
Examine the definition of prophethood
Identify the key components: inspiration, recipient conditions, and the various 'whether or not' clauses that define its scope.
Compare with the definition of messengership which adds the condition of conveyance.
3
Understand the refutation of acquisition
The passage uses the consensus of Muslims and the 'even if climbing the highest mountain' analogy to reject the philosophers' claim.
The climbing analogy emphasizes that no amount of difficult worship can earn prophethood.
4
Grasp the concept of divine favor
Focus on the second verse: 'Rather, that is the favor of Allah; He gives it to whom He wills.' The commentary explains favor as giving without any compensation.
This reinforces the core idea that prophethood is purely a gift.

تعريفُ النُّبوة، وبيان أنَّ النُّبوَّة محضُ تَفضُّلٍ مِن الله
وَلَمْ تَكُنْ نُبُوَّةٌ مُكْتَسَبَهُ وَلَوْ رَقَى فِي الخَيرِ أَعْلَى عَقَبَهْ
ولمَّا جوَّزَ الفلاسفةُ اكتساب النُّبوَّة بملازمة الخلوة والعبادة وتناول الحلال ، أشار إلى الرَّدِّ عليهم بقوله : (وَ) مذهب أهل الحق أَنَّه لَمْ تَكُنْ وهي ، نُبوَّة) شرعاً: إيحاء الله تعالى لإنسان عاقل حُرِّ ذَكرٍ، بحكم شرعي تكليفي، سواءٌ أمره بتبليغه أم لا ، كان معه كتاب أم لا ، كان له شرع مجدد أم لا ، كان له نسخ لشرع من قبله أو بعضه أم لا ، وكذا الرسالة إلا في اشتراط التبليغ فإنَّه لا بُدَّ مِنه في مفهومها ، والمراد أنَّ النُّبوَّة بحسب ما عُلم مِن القواعد الدينية وانعقد عليه إجماع المسلمين لم تكن (مُكْتَسَبَة) أي: لا تُنال بمجرَّد الكسب بالجد والاجتهاد، ومباشرة أسباب مخصوصة كما زعمه الفلاسفة (وَلَوْ رَقَى فِي الخَيْرِ أَعَلَى) أي: أَبْعِدَ (عَقَبَة) وهي في الأصل: الطَّريق الصاعد في الجبل ، أريد منه هنا : أشقُّ الطَّاعات وأفضلها ، أي: ولو اقتحم العبد أشقّ العبادات المُشبَّهة لمشقّتها رُقي العقبات.
بَلْ ذَاكَ فَضْلُ اللَّهِ يُؤْتِيهِ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ جَلَّ اللهُ واهِبُ المِنَنْ
(بَلْ ذَاكَ) أي اصطفاءُ النَّبي للنباة واختياره للرسالة (فَضْلُ اللهِ) أي: أثرُ جُودِه وإنعامه، والفضل : إعطاء الشَّيء بغير عوض لا عاجل ولا آجلٍ ، ولذا لا يكون لغيره تعالى (يُؤْتِيهِ) بمحض اختياره (لمَنْ يَشَاءُ) ممَّنْ ...
Definition of prophethood, and explanation that prophethood is pure favor from Allah. And there was no prophethood acquired, even if one ascends in goodness the highest mountain path. And when the philosophers allowed the acquisition of prophethood by maintaining seclusion, worship, and consuming lawful things, he pointed to the refutation of them by his saying: (And) the doctrine of the People of Truth is that it was not, and it is, prophethood legally: the inspiration of Allah the Exalted to a rational, free, male human being, with a legislative ruling that is obligatory, whether He commands him to convey it or not, whether there is with him a book or not, whether he has a renewed law or not, whether he abrogates a previous law or part of it or not, and likewise messengership except in the condition of conveyance, for it is necessary in its concept. And the intent is that prophethood, according to what is known from religious principles and the consensus of the Muslims, was not acquired, i.e., it is not attained merely by striving and diligence and engaging in specific causes as the philosophers claimed. (And even if he ascends in goodness the highest) i.e., the furthest (mountain path), which originally means the ascending road in the mountain; intended here: the most difficult and best acts of obedience, i.e., even if the servant undertakes the most difficult acts of worship, likened in their difficulty to climbing mountain paths. Rather, that is the favor of Allah; He gives it to whom He wills, exalted is Allah, the Bestower of favors. (Rather, that) i.e., the selection of the prophet [for prophethood] and his choice for messengership (is the favor of Allah) i.e., the effect of His generosity and beneficence. And favor: giving something without recompense, neither immediate nor deferred; therefore it cannot be from other than Him. (He gives it) by His mere choice (to whom He wills) from among ...
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage defines prophethood and refutes the philosophical view that it can be acquired. The author begins by stating the title: 'Definition of prophethood, and explanation that prophethood is pure favor from Allah.' He then quotes the first verse: 'And there was no prophethood acquired, even if one ascends in goodness the highest mountain path.' The commentary explains that the philosophers claimed prophethood can be attained through seclusion, worship, and lawful food, so the verse refutes them. The refutation includes a detailed definition of prophethood: it is divine inspiration to a rational, free, male human being with a legislative ruling, regardless of whether he is commanded to convey it, whether he has a book, whether he brings a new law or abrogates a previous one. Messengership is similar but requires conveyance. Then the commentary emphasizes that according to religious principles and consensus of Muslims, prophethood is not acquired; it is not attained by effort or specific practices, no matter how difficult the acts of worship, likened to climbing a steep mountain path. The second verse states: 'Rather, that is the favor of Allah; He gives it to whom He wills...' The commentary explains that 'that' refers to the selection of the prophet for prophethood and messengership. 'Favor' is giving without any compensation, immediate or deferred, so it belongs only to Allah. Thus, prophethood is purely a divine gift, given by His mere choice to whomever He wills.

Key Terms
النبوة
مكتسبة
فضل الله
إيحاء
إجماع المسلمين
الفلاسفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophethood can be attained through extreme worship, seclusion, and lawful living.
Correction: Prophethood is a pure divine gift; no amount of human effort can earn it. It is solely by Allah's choice and favor.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consensus of the Muslims regarding prophethood?
A) It can be acquired through extreme worship and seclusion.
B) It is not acquired and cannot be attained by effort.
C) It is attainable only by those with high intelligence.
D) It is a natural result of moral perfection.

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is a divine gift (فضل الله) given solely by Allah's choice, not achievable through human effort.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel your worships and efforts are not yielding the closeness to Allah you desire, do you become frustrated or do you realize that it is Allah's favor that He grants as He wills? How might this shift your prayer today?
?
Is there any area of your life where you act as if you can earn Allah's special favor through your own righteousness, forgetting that prophethood and all guidance are pure gifts? How will you humble yourself before Him in that area starting now?
?
If prophethood—the highest station—cannot be earned, then how should that dissolve your pride in your own piety? What would it look like for you to live today with the deep conviction that everything good you have is a gift, not a wage?

Definition of Prophethood and Its Divine Origin
The author defines prophethood and refutes the claim it is acquired.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of prophethood and why it is a divine favor, not a status attained through human effort.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a divine gift, not a human achievement.

What makes a person a prophet? Is it extreme piety, rigorous effort, or something entirely beyond human reach? In this passage, Sanusi defines prophethood and clarifies its divine origin, refuting the philosophical claim that it can be attained through exertion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with a definition and then clarifies it.
2
Understand the definition
Identify the two key elements: prophethood is a pure favor from Allah, and conveying (tabligh) is essential to its concept.
3
Recognize the refutation
The passage explicitly denies that prophethood is acquired (muktasaba) through effort or specific means. Note the reference to philosophers.
4
Examine the illustration
The phrase 'even if he ascended in goodness higher (a mountain pass)' shows that even the most difficult worship cannot earn prophethood.
The mountain pass metaphor emphasizes extreme difficulty.
5
Conclude with the divine favor
The passage ends by affirming that prophethood is solely Allah's favor, given to whom He wills.
This reinforces the main point: it is not acquired.

It then explains the phrase 'even if he ascended in goodness higher (a mountain pass)' to illustrate that even if a person performs the most difficult acts of worship, they cannot attain prophethood by themselves. Finally, it concludes that prophethood is purely a favor from Allah, given to whom He wills, affirming that He is the Bestower of gifts.

Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation without any exception.

It includes everything: celestial, terrestrial, humans, jinn, angels, this world and the Hereafter.
