The Absolute Superiority of the Prophet
The commentator proves that Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creatures absolutely.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural basis for the absolute superiority of Prophet Muhammad over all creation, including angels and jinn.

Core Idea
Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creation; this is a matter of consensus and explicit proof.

This lesson examines a key claim in Islamic theology: the absolute superiority of the Prophet over all creatures. The commentator unpacks the poetic verse by defining its terms, establishing consensus, and providing scriptural proof. You will see how this doctrine is grounded in both hadith and Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the poetic line and explanation
Start by reading the Arabic verse and its literal translation. Notice how the commentator breaks down each word.
The verse is from the Jawharat al-Tawhid.
2
Understand 'ala al-itlaq' (absolutely)
Focus on the meaning of 'absolute' superiority: it covers all creation, every realm, and all times.
This universality is crucial to the claim.
3
Recognize the consensus
See how the commentator states that this superiority is a matter of consensus (ijma) among Muslims.
This consensus is an exception to the angel-humans debate.
4
Examine the two proofs
Read the hadith: 'I am the most honored...' and the Quranic verse: 'You are the best community.' Understand how they prove the Prophet's superiority.
The second proof links the Prophet's rank to his community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦٥ - وَأَفْضَلُ الخَلْقِ عَلَى الإِطْلَاقِ نَبِيِّنَا فَمِلْ عَنِ الشَّقَاقِ
(وَأَفْضَلُ) (الخَلْقِ) أي: المخلوقات (عَلَى الإِطْلَاقِ) المراد جميع العموم الشامل للعلوية والسفليّة من البشر والجِنِّ والمَلك في الدُّنيا والآخرة في سائر خلال الخير ونعوت الكمال ( نَبِيُّنَا) محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ، والإضافة منه فيه لتشريف المضاف إليه، لا للاختصاص؛ لما سيأتي من عموم بعثته، وإن جعل الضمير للمكلَّفين كان عاما مطابقا له، وأفضليته على جميع المخلوقات مما أجمعَ عليه المسلمون، وهو مستثنى من الخلاف في التفضيل بين الملك والبشر، لقوله: «أنا أكرم الأوّلين والآخرين على الله؛ ولا فخر» ولأنَّ أمَّته أفضل الأمم؛ لقوله تعالى: كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ
65. And the best of creation absolutely is our Prophet, so turn away from disagreement. (And the best) (of creation) meaning: created beings (absolutely) meaning: all universality encompassing the higher and lower realms of humans, jinn, and angels in this world and the Hereafter in all virtues and perfect attributes. (our Prophet) Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. The attribution (of the pronoun) to him is for honor of the one attributed to, not for exclusivity; because of what will come of the universality of his mission. And if the pronoun is made for the morally responsible, it would be general matching him. And his superiority over all created beings is a matter of consensus among Muslims, and it is exempted from the disagreement about superiority between angels and humans, because of his saying: 'I am the most honored of the first and the last before God, and I say this not out of pride,' and because his community is the best of communities, due to His saying: 'You are the best community.'
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the absolute superiority of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) over all creation. The commentator begins by explaining the poetic line: 'And the best of creation absolutely is our Prophet, so turn away from disagreement.' He defines each term: 'al-khalq' means all created beings, including humans, jinn, and angels. 'Ala al-itlaq' indicates complete universality—encompassing every realm, both higher (heavens) and lower (earth), in this world and the next, covering all virtues and perfect attributes. The attribution 'nabiyyuna' (our Prophet) specifically refers to Muhammad. The commentator clarifies that the possessive construction (our Prophet) is for honoring the community of believers by their relation to him, not to imply that he was sent exclusively to them, because later it will be shown that his mission is universal. If the pronoun 'our' refers to all morally responsible beings (including previous nations and angels), it would still be inclusive and match the universality. Then the commentator asserts that the superiority of the Prophet over all creatures is a matter of consensus (ijma') among Muslims. This consensus is an exception to the existing disagreement about whether angels or humans are superior in general—i.e., regardless of that dispute, the Prophet is undoubtedly superior to all. Two proofs are given: first, the Prophet's own statement: 'I am the most honored of the first and the last before God, and I say this not out of pride'—this hadith shows his unique rank. Second, the superiority of his community (ummah) as stated in the Quran: 'You are the best community' indicates by extension that their Prophet is the best of prophets.

Key Terms
الخَلْق
الإِطْلَاق
الإضافة
الأفضلية
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the phrase 'our Prophet' limits his mission to Muslims.
Correction: The commentator explains that the possessive is for honor, not exclusivity; his mission is universal.

Checkpoint
What does 'ala al-itlaq' (absolutely) mean in this passage?
A) That the Prophet is superior to all humans in the world only.
B) That his superiority encompasses all created beings without restriction in time, place, or kind.
C) That the Prophet is superior only to angels and not to other prophets.
D) That his superiority is limited to the Hereafter.

Key Takeaway
Prophet Muhammad is the absolute best of all creation, proven by consensus and explicit texts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely treat the Prophet as the absolute best of all creation in your daily choices, or do you sometimes put personal desires and worldly pursuits above his teachings? What one concrete action can you take today to honor his rank above everything else?
?
The Prophet said he is the most honored without pride. Are you proud of being part of his community merely by lineage or culture, while your actions lag behind? How can you humble yourself and sincerely strive to embody his character as the best of creation?
?
If his community is the best of communities, what specific responsibility does that place on you? Do you live in a way that reflects this honor, or do you blend in with those who disregard it? Commit to one visible change this week that distinguishes you as a member of the best community.

The Prophet's Superiority: Consensus and Proofs
States the Prophet's superiority, asserts consensus, and provides textual proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet Muhammad's superiority over all creatures is a matter of Muslim consensus, supported by his own statement and the Quran, and that it is an exception to the general debate between angels and humans.

Core Idea
The Prophet is the best of all creation by consensus and divine texts.

After clarifying the grammatical point of the pronoun addition, the author now asserts a central tenet of Ahl al-Sunna: the absolute superiority of Prophet Muhammad over all creatures. He grounds this claim in both consensus and explicit textual proofs, and clarifies that this settled matter is not affected by the debate over whether angels are superior to humans generally.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on superiority

The passage includes the phrase 'مما أجمعَ عليه المسلمون'.

Understand the consensus and exception
The author says this is a matter of consensus and that it is an exception to the disagreement about angels vs humans. Why is this exception important?
It settles the debate for the case of the Prophet.
3
Examine the proofs
The Prophet's own hadith and the Quranic verse about his nation being the best are the proofs. Reflect on how these establish his superiority.
The hadith is 'أنا أكرم الأولين والآخرين على الله'.

فيه لتشريف المضاف إليه (۱) ، لا للاختصاص (۲) ؛ لما سيأتي من عموم بعثته ، وإن جعل الضمير للمكلَّفين كان عاما مطابقا له (۳) ، وأفضليته على جميع المخلوقات مما أجمعَ عليه المسلمون ، وهو مستثنى من الخلاف في التفضيل بين الملك والبشر (٤) ، لقوله : «أنا أكرم الأولين والآخرين على الله ولا فخر (٥) (٦) ولأن أمته أفضل الأمم : لقوله تعالى: كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ
Statement that the best of all creatures is our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him. In it (the pronoun) is for honoring the one to whom it is annexed (1), not for exclusivity (2); because of the generality of his mission that will come. And if the pronoun is made for the responsible ones (mukallafin), it would be general consistent with it (3). And his superiority over all creatures is something on which the Muslims are united (in consensus) (4). And it is excepted from the disagreement about preference between angel and human (4). Due to his saying: 'I am the most honored of the first and the last before Allah, and I say this not out of pride (5)(6)', and because his nation is the best of nations, due to the Almighty's saying: 'You are the best nation...'
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the Prophet's superiority. It begins by stating that the pronoun in the preceding text (the context) is for honoring the nation (the annexed), not for specifying that the Prophet was sent only to them, because his mission is general. Then it asserts that his superiority over all creation is a matter of consensus among Muslims, and it is an exception to the debate about whether angels are superior to humans or vice versa. The proof is the Prophet's own statement that he is the most honored and his nation being called the best nation in the Quran.

Key Terms
أفضل المخلوقات
الإجماع
التفضيل بين الملك والبشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the Prophet's superiority an exception to the disagreement about angels and humans?
A) Because angels are superior to humans anyway.
B) Because the Prophet is superior to all creatures by consensus and explicit texts.
C) Because the debate only applies to ordinary humans.
D) Because the Prophet is not human.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad is the best of all creatures, a matter of consensus, supported by his own statement and the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet is the best of all creation. Is your love for him reflected in your daily priorities? When you face a choice between following his sunnah and following your own desire, which one truly decides your action? Are you willing to examine your life and identify one area where you consistently prefer your own way over his?
?
The author says the Prophet's superiority is a matter of consensus among Muslims. But if you are honest, do you sometimes act as if other people's opinions or your own preferences hold more weight than what the Prophet commanded? Think of a specific example where you have compromised a prophetic teaching for a worldly gain. What would it cost you to rectify that today?
?
The Quran declares this Ummah the best nation because it follows the Prophet. Does your participation in this Ummah—your prayers, your charity, your character—actually reflect that you are part of the best nation? Or are you just a nominal Muslim? What one concrete step can you take this week to make your life a truer testimony to the Prophet's superiority?

The Pronoun Addition: For Honor, Not Exclusivity
Explains the purpose of the pronoun addition in the phrase 'our Prophet'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the pronoun in the phrase 'our Prophet' indicates honor for his nation, not that his mission was limited to them.

Core Idea
The pronoun addition honors the nation, not restricts the mission.

Before proving the Prophet's universal mission later in the text, the author addresses a grammatical point: the use of the possessive pronoun in 'our Prophet' (نبينا). He explains that this construction is meant to honor the nation (the annexed noun) by associating them with the Prophet, not to indicate that the Prophet was sent only to them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on pronoun addition
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note the two possibilities: the pronoun is for honor or for exclusivity.
The author explicitly says it is not for exclusivity.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why does the author reject exclusivity? Because later he will mention the generality of his mission. Also, if the pronoun referred to the 'responsible ones' (mukallafin) it would be general and consistent.
The phrase 'لما سيأتي من عموم بعثته' refers to a later point in the text.
3
Appreciate the significance
This detail shows the author's care in language: even a pronoun can be misinterpreted. He clarifies to avoid the misunderstanding that the Prophet was only sent to his nation.
The common misunderstanding is that the pronoun indicates exclusivity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أن أفضل المخلوقات جميعها هو نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
فيه لتشريف المضاف إليه (۱) ، لا للاختصاص (۲) ؛ لما سيأتي من عموم بعثته ، وإن جعل الضمير للمكلَّفين كان عاما مطابقا له (۳) ، وأفضليته على جميع المخلوقات مما أجمعَ عليه المسلمون ، وهو مستثنى من الخلاف في التفضيل بين الملك والبشر (٤) ، لقوله : «أنا أكرم الأولين والآخرين على الله ولا فخر (٥) (٦) ولأن أمته أفضل الأمم : لقوله تعالى: كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ
Statement that the best of all creatures is our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him. In it (the pronoun) is for honoring the one to whom it is annexed (1), not for exclusivity (2); because of the generality of his mission that will come. And if the pronoun is made for the responsible ones (mukallafin), it would be general consistent with it (3). And his superiority over all creatures is something on which the Muslims are united (in consensus) (4). And it is excepted from the disagreement about preference between angel and human (4). Due to his saying: 'I am the most honored of the first and the last before Allah, and I say this not out of pride (5)(6)', and because his nation is the best of nations, due to the Almighty's saying: 'You are the best nation...'

It begins by stating that the pronoun in the preceding text (the context) is for honoring the nation (the annexed), not for specifying that the Prophet was sent only to them, because his mission is general. Then it asserts that his superiority over all creation is a matter of consensus among Muslims, and it is an exception to the debate about whether angels are superior to humans or vice versa. The proof is the Prophet's own statement that he is the most honored and his nation being called the best nation in the Quran.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The possessive pronoun 'our' in 'our Prophet' indicates that the Prophet was sent only to that nation (exclusivity).
Correction: The author clarifies it is for honor, not exclusivity, as evidenced by the universal mission.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the purpose of the pronoun addition (إضافة الضمير) in the text?
A) To specify that the Prophet was sent only to his nation.
B) To honor his nation by associating them with him.
C) To indicate that the Prophet is superior to all creatures.
D) To exclude angels from the discussion.

Key Takeaway
The possessive pronoun in 'our Prophet' honors the nation, not limits the mission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'our Prophet', do you feel a sense of honor that also demands you to share his message with others, or do you treat it as a exclusive title that lets you feel superior to those outside the faith?
?
If the pronoun in 'our Prophet' is for honoring the nation, how does that honor reflect on your daily actions? Are you living in a way that brings honor to the one who said, 'I have been sent to all of mankind'?
?
Knowing that the universality of his mission means non-Muslims are also included in his prophethood, what is one concrete step you will take this week to convey a part of his message to someone who has not yet accepted it?

Refutation of the Claim that Jibril is Superior to the Prophet
Refutes Zamakhshari's claim that Jibril is superior to Prophet Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly refutation of al-Zamakhshari's argument for Jibril's superiority over Prophet Muhammad, based on Quranic context and the principle that a student can be superior to the teacher.

Core Idea
A teacher (Jibril) is not necessarily superior to the student (the Prophet).

This passage confronts a specific claim made by al-Zamakhshari in his tafsir, that the angel Jibril is superior to Prophet Muhammad. The author dismisses it as unworthy of mention, then provides a detailed refutation quoting al-Qadi al-Baydawi and adding a logical point about the relationship between teacher and taught. You will see how careful attention to Quranic context and sound reasoning dismantles this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get a sense of the argument's flow.
Note how the author begins by dismissing the claim outright.
2
Understand al-Baydawi's refutation
Al-Baydawi explains that the verses in al-Takwir are not comparing virtues but rebutting accusations. Identify the key phrase where he states the intended purpose.
3
Grasp the 'mu'allam' argument
Even if Jibril taught the Prophet, the student can be superior. Reflect on examples where a teacher is lesser than the student.
The term 'mu'allam' (فتح) refers to the one being taught.
4
Connect to broader 'ilm al-kalam principles
This shows that rank in creation is not determined by role alone. Prophethood is a higher station than angelic status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا عبرة بما ادعاه الزمخشري مِن أن جبريل أفضل من نبينا ، قال العلامة الأمير: ولا ينبغي أن يذكر، وفي تفسير القاضي البيضاوي لقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّهُ لَقَوْلُ رَسُولِ كَرِيمٍ ذِى قُوَّة عِندَ ذِي الْعَرْشِ مَكِينِ ﴾ [التكوير : ١٩ - ٢٠] ما نصه: «واستدل - أي: الزمخشري ـ بذلك على فضل جبريل على سيدنا محمد عليهما الصلاة والسلام، حيث عد فضائل جبريل واقتصر على نفي الجنون عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وهو ضعيف، إذ المقصود منه نفي قولهم: ﴿إِنَّمَا يُعَلِّمُهُ بَشَر [النحل: ١٠٣] وأَفتَرَى عَلَى اللَّهِ كَذِبًا أَم بِهِ جِنَّةٌ بَلِ الَّذِينَ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ بِالْآخِرَةِ فِي الْعَذَابِ وَالضَّلَلِ الْبَعِيدِ ﴾ [سبأ: ٨] وليس المقصود تعداد فضلهما والموازنة بينهما» وبما تُوهِم فضل جبريل أيضا من أنه يعلمه ، وكم من مُعلَّم - بالفتح - أفضل ممن يعلمه. الأمير والشنواني.
And no consideration is given to what al-Zamakhshari claimed that Jibril is superior to our Prophet. Al-Allama al-Amir said: It should not even be mentioned. And in the Tafsir of al-Qadi al-Baydawi on the Almighty's saying: {Indeed, it is the speech of a noble messenger, endowed with power, established before the Lord of the Throne} (al-Takwir 19-20) is his text: 'He (al-Zamakhshari) used that as evidence for Jibril's superiority over our master Muhammad, peace be upon them both, since he listed Jibril's virtues and confined himself to negating insanity from the Prophet, and this is weak, because the intended purpose (of the verse) is to negate their saying: {He is only taught by a human} (al-Nahl 103) and {He has fabricated a lie against Allah or is there madness in him?} (al-Saba' 8), and it is not intended to enumerate their virtues and weigh between them.' And also by what gives the impression of Jibril's superiority from the fact that he teaches him, but how many a taught one (mu'allam, with fatha) is better than his teacher. Al-Amir and al-Shanawani.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific claim. It begins by dismissing al-Zamakhshari's claim that Jibril is superior as unworthy of mention, citing al-Amir. Then it quotes al-Qadi al-Baydawi's Tafsir, which explains that the context of the verses in Surah al-Takwir is not to compare their virtues but to rebut the disbelievers' accusations. The claim that Jibril's role as teacher implies superiority is refuted by noting that the taught one can be superior to the teacher.

Key Terms
الزمخشري
جبريل
تفضيل
القاضي البيضاوي
مُعلَّم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jibril is superior to Prophet Muhammad because he is a higher angel and taught the Prophet.
Correction: The Quranic verses used are not comparative; the role of teacher does not imply superiority; the Prophet's rank is higher.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is al-Zamakhshari's argument from the verses in al-Takwir considered weak?
A) Because the verses actually prove Jibril's superiority.
B) Because the verses are not intended to compare their virtues, but to refute the disbelievers' accusations.
C) Because the Prophet never claimed superiority.
D) Because the verses are abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The claim that Jibril is superior to the Prophet is unfounded and contradicted by Quranic context and sound reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you assumed that someone in a position of authority or teaching is automatically superior to you in knowledge or status? How did that assumption affect your learning and your relationship with that person? What will you do to correct this?
?
This lesson shows that even a revered teacher (Jibril) can be less than the student (Prophet). Who do you look up to so much that you forget the possibility that they might not be superior to you in Allah’s sight? How will you recalibrate your respect and emulation?
?
Are you more focused on the titles and roles of people (e.g., teacher, scholar) or on the truth they convey? This week, catch yourself comparing based on status and replace it with seeking the truth regardless of the messenger.

Proof of Prophet Muhammad's Superiority from Quran and Hadith
Proof and ruling from Quran and Hadith on Prophet's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran and hadith affirm the Prophet's superiority over all prophets, and the obligation to believe this.

Core Idea
The best of nations implies the best of prophets; hadiths of equality are out of humility.

This passage tackles a central belief: that Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is the best of all prophets. It uses Quranic verses describing the Muslim nation as the best to indirectly affirm his superiority. Then it addresses hadiths that seem to forbid preferring him, explaining their true meaning. The passage concludes with the clear ruling that denying this superiority is sinful and renders one an innovator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how it combines Quranic proof, hadith explanation, and a ruling.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the Quranic proof
The passage cites two verses to show the Muslim nation is the best (خير أمة) and a middle/just nation. It then argues that the nation's goodness depends on the prophet's perfection. So praising the nation indirectly praises the prophet.
This is the core logical argument.
3
Analyze the hadiths about preference
The hadiths 'Do not prefer me over Moses' and 'Do not give preference between prophets' are explained. Their meaning is to prohibit a type of preference that leads to diminishing others, not to negate his superiority.
The passage offers two possible interpretations: either the Prophet said this before knowing his superiority (dismissed as weak) or out of politeness/humility.
4
Learn the ruling on deniers
The passage states that it is obligatory (واجب) to believe he is the best. The denier disobeys, is considered an innovator, and is to be disciplined. This is a strong theological stance.
This shows the seriousness of this belief in Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم النبوات
أُخْرِجَتْ لِلنَّاسِ [آل عمران: ۱۱۰] . ﴿وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطام (البقرة: ١٤٣]، أي: عدولاً وخيارًا ، ولا شكّ أنَّ خيريَّة الأمم إنَّما هي بحسب كمالها في الدين، وذلك تابع لكمال نبيّها الذي تتبعه (۱)، فتفضيلها تفضيل له ، وأما قوله : «لا تخيروني على موسى» (۲) و «لا تفضّلوا بين الأنبياء»(۳) ونحوه ؛ فمعناه: لا تخيروني تخيير مُفاضلة (٤) ، ولا يُحتاج إلى أنه قال ذلك قبل أن يَعلَم أَنَّه أفضل ، لأنَّه مجرَّد احتمال كما قاله ابن أَقْبَرْس(٥)، ويحتمل أنه قاله تأدبا وتواضعاً، فالواجب على كلِّ مكلَّف اعتقاد أنه أفضل الجميع، فيعصي منكره (٦) ، ويُبدع ويؤدب.
Section of Prophethoods. Brought forth for mankind (Al 'Imran 110). {And thus we made you a middle nation} (al-Baqarah 143), that is, just and chosen. And there is no doubt that the goodness of nations is only according to their perfection in religion, and that is dependent on the perfection of their prophet whom they follow (1). So preferring them is a preference for him. As for his saying: 'Do not prefer me over Moses' (2) and 'Do not give preference between the prophets' (3) and similar, its meaning is: do not prefer me with a preference of comparison (that leads to diminishing others) (4). And there is no need to (say) that he said that before he knew that he was superior, because it is a mere possibility, as Ibn Aqbars said (5). And it is possible that he said it out of politeness and humility. So it is obligatory upon every responsible person (mukallaf) to believe that he is the best of all, so his denier disobeys (6), and is considered an innovator and is disciplined.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is a proof and an imperative ruling. It begins by citing Quranic verses that describe the Muslim nation as the best and a middle nation, then argues that the perfection of a nation derives from the perfection of its prophet, so the nation's preference is a preference for the prophet. It then addresses the hadiths that seem to prohibit preferring the Prophet over other prophets, explaining that they forbid a type of preference that implies diminishment or leads to conflict, not the recognition of his superiority. The claim that he said this before knowing his own superiority is dismissed as a mere possibility. The passage concludes with the ruling: it is obligatory to believe he is the best, and whoever denies this commits sin, is considered an innovator, and is to be disciplined.

Key Terms
خير أمة
أمة وسط
لا تخيروني على موسى
لا تفضلوا بين الأنبياء
مفاضلة
ابن أقبرس
تأدب
إبداع
تأديب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the hadith 'Do not prefer me over Moses' proves that no prophet is superior, so it is not obligatory to believe in the Prophet's superiority over others.
Correction: The passage explains that the hadith prohibits a specific type of preference (مفاضلة) that leads to diminishing others or conflict, not the recognition of his actual superiority. The obligation to believe he is the best remains.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on someone who denies that the Prophet is the best of all creation?
A) He is considered a disbeliever.
B) He is considered an innovator and is to be disciplined.
C) He is excused if he is ignorant.
D) He does not incur sin because the matter is disputed.

Key Takeaway
It is obligatory to believe that Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is the best of all prophets; denying this is a sin and marks one as an innovator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone downplay the status of Prophet Muhammad ﷺ compared to other prophets, do you feel a strong urge to correct them, or do you stay silent? What does your response reveal about the depth of your conviction in his superiority?
?
Is there any part of your heart that hesitates to fully believe that the Prophet ﷺ is the best of all creation, perhaps out of a misguided sense of 'fairness' to other prophets? How can you uproot that hesitation today?
?
The passage states that denying the Prophet's superiority is an innovation and leads to discipline. If you have ever harbored doubt about this, will you now resolve to study and affirm this belief with certainty, even if it means confronting your own previous assumptions?
